Important News Two

Hangzhou Northern Expedition 47

Memorial Tower for Fallen Soldiers Completed

The Memorial Tower for Fallen Soldiers of the Northern Expedition in Hangzhou, west of Lake, was laid in place on November 12th, the 17th year. After a year and six months, the entire project has finally been completed. The total construction cost is roughly 18,000 yuan. The completion ceremony will be held this morning (1st) at 9:00 a.m. The provincial Executive Committee sent invitations in advance to various agencies and organizations in the city to participate, so the number of attendees was very high. The event was chaired by Chen Xihao of the Provincial Executive Committee, and the order was as follows: (1) Stand at attention, (2) Play music, (3) Unveiling, (4) Sing the Party song, (5) Pay the highest respects to the national flag, the Party flag, the General’s portrait, and the spirit tablets of the fallen soldiers of the Northern Expedition of the National Revolutionary Army, (6) The chairman respectfully reads the General’s will, (7) Moment of silence, (8) Chairman delivers the opening speech, (9) Speeches, (10) Play music, (11) Photography, (12) Adjournment. The construction of the tower was quite extensive. All the white, black, and tricolor marble was purchased from Italy. The sides of the tower used Jinshan stone from Suzhou and red stone from Ningbo. The top of the tower is inlaid with enamel square tiles. The tower inscription used stones from Quzhou and electric lights were installed around the perimeter. The tower has four reliefs: one depicting the oath-taking ceremony of the Northern Expedition, one depicting the armed forces of the people, one depicting the recapture of Wuhan, and one depicting peace and construction. The design of the artwork is still in progress.

Guangdong Province to Abolish Likin in October 48

Gambling Banned Only After Military Operations End

Entry Tax on Fruit Products Abolished by Explicit Order

Guangzhou Correspondence: The National Government has explicitly ordered the abolition of likin throughout the country on October 10th of this year and has telegraphed the financial commissioners and finance departments of various provinces to prepare plans for abolishing likin in their respective provinces. Specialists, carrying plans, will be sent to Beijing before May 30th to discuss everything in person. The provinces were also ordered to telegraph Beijing in advance for verification of the total annual income of all likin taxes and similar likin taxes, broken down into individual items and total amounts. The Guangdong provincial finance authorities have reported all likin and similar likin taxes in the province to the provincial government. As for gambling, it will be banned only after military operations are completely concluded. The provincial government, based on the report, consulted the Ministry of Interior yesterday, stating, "[We now acknowledge your ministry's Police Character No. 321 consultation stating that the Secretariat of the Executive Yuan has forwarded a letter from Party member Li Yaohuan requesting the removal of customs barriers and likin and the prohibition of opium and gambling, and requested that it be handled separately. In addition, we have copied the section attached by Party member Li Yaohuan on prohibiting opium and gambling to eliminate the source of chaos and ensure the livelihood of the people. Upon investigation, we found that the Anti-Opium Commission previously sent a consultation with similar content, which was ordered to be reviewed and reported by the Finance Department and then forwarded for review. The Finance Department replied, 'Regarding the abolition of likin, the Finance Department received an order from your office No. 354 in February of this year, and the Executive Yuan approved a letter from the Civil Service Department of the National Government, which ordered that from October 10th of this year, all likin and similar likin taxes throughout the country will be abolished. We should comply with this order and implement it when the time comes. As for gambling, due to the ongoing suppression of the rebellion and the urgent need for funds, we have no choice but to rely on gambling revenue to meet the expenses. Once the military operations are concluded, we will ban it. The prohibition of opium is under the jurisdiction of the Guangdong Anti-Opium Bureau, and the Finance Department cannot comment on it. Due to the previous orders, we have reported to your office for review and await further instructions.' We believe that the reliance on gambling revenue to maintain military expenses is a factual situation and should be forwarded to the Anti-Opium Commission for review. As the Anti-Opium Bureau is under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Finance, whether it should be prohibited and should be reviewed by the Ministry of Finance and then instructed to the Finance Department for notification and forwarded to the Anti-Opium Commission for review. Based on the previous consultation, we have written a document reporting the handling situation and hope you will review it. Currently, the annual income from various likin taxes in Guangdong Province is approximately 5.7 million yuan. The fees for sitting likin platforms is approximately 1.5 million yuan. The various government and county taxes similar to likin is approximately 1.62 million yuan. The Guangdong financial commissioner and the finance department director Fan Qiwu have telegraphed the Ministry of Finance to verify this. Recently, the Finance Department has begun to abolish these likin taxes based on their urgency. The Guangzhou Municipal Government has a collection of taxes on fruits, which have been collected since the 20th of this month, after the contract with the merchants expired, has been explicitly canceled by the Finance Department and will no longer be contracted to merchants. (May 26th)"

Recent Financial Situation in Guangdong Province 49

Decision to Redeem Principal and Pay Interest on Military Treasury Bonds Next Month

Bank of China Implements Exchange for 100 Yuan Banknotes

Guangzhou Correspondence: Recently, with the conclusion of the war in Guangxi Province, a comfortable situation has suddenly emerged in Guangdong's financial circles. In the past, during the military period, the Bank of China's banknotes experienced several storms, and only the one-yuan banknotes could be fully used in the market. The remaining five-yuan, ten-yuan, fifty-yuan, and up to one hundred-yuan banknotes were discounted to seventy percent. During the military period, the total value of banknotes above five yuan could not exceed the aforementioned price. Now that the war has ended, most bankers believe that the war has come to an end, and the political situation will stabilize accordingly. Therefore, they are collecting the Bank of China's five-yuan and other denominations at high prices. Manipulators are taking advantage of the opportunity to raise their value. As a result, five-yuan and above Bank of China banknotes gradually increased from seventy percent to ninety percent as of yesterday (the 23rd). The main reason for the financial community to raise the price of Bank of China banknotes is that the government recently decided to implement lottery redemption of principal and interest for the issued military treasury bonds next month (June). At the same time, maturing treasury bonds will also be paid in full. In order to cope with the payment of the above treasury bonds, the government had no choice but to first restore the redemption of central banknotes above one yuan in order to facilitate turnover. Speculators predicted this trend and judged that the government would inevitably issue a policy to restore the redemption of banknotes above one yuan. Therefore, they scrambled to collect them, and as a result, the Bank of China notes above five yuan have continued to increase in value for days, from seventy percent to ninety percent. Now that this phenomenon exists, the government will not have much difficulty in preparing cash, even if it implements the restoration of any kind of banknote. First, Fan Qiwu, the Director of the Department of Finance of the Provincial Government, Huang Jusu, Sun Xiwu, and Qu Guoqiang, the Governor of the Bank of China, were dispatched by the Provincial Government to prepare for the redemption of Bank of China banknotes. Yesterday, the Provincial Government issued a clear order to the Department of Finance and the Bank of China to first restore the redemption of one hundred-yuan banknotes on the 26th. The remaining five-yuan, ten-yuan, and fifty-yuan Bank of China banknotes will also be redeemed successively in the shortest possible time. After the one-hundred-yuan banknotes are redeemed, the five-yuan and ten-yuan banknotes can also be redeemed in succession within five or six days. (May 24th)

Chen Peikun, Gan Yun, and Others Arrive in Fujian 50

Fuzhou Correspondence: Chen Peikun recently went to Shanghai from Xiamen, and then returned to Fujian from Shanghai. It is said that when Chen passed through Xiamen, he negotiated a loan of 70,000 yuan with various parties, using the consolidated consumer goods bureau as collateral. Three thousand yuan has already been delivered, and the remaining 40,000 yuan will be remitted successively. The political expenses to be issued for the Dragon Boat Festival are only 50,000 yuan short. The military expenses are handled by the Special Finance Office. As for Chen's concurrent positions as Director of Civil Affairs and Director of Finance, it is said that if the central government and Chairman Yang urge him further, he may reluctantly take on the position of Director of Civil Affairs. However, since Li Chengyi's resignation as Director of Finance has not yet been approved, he should be urged to come to Fujian immediately to avoid interruption of government affairs.

The newly appointed Party Commissioners Gan Yun, Chen Lianfang, and Kang Shaozhou also arrived in the province yesterday. It is heard that Gan and others will start by sorting out the Party affairs in Fujian Province in the future, so that the Provincial Party Headquarters can be formally established as soon as possible. Since the Party Headquarters in Fujian Province has been openly active since the 15th year of the Republic of China, it is still in the preparatory period. The central government hopes that the Provincial Party Headquarters will be completed soon. As for the local Party Headquarters in various counties, whether they have been formally established or are still in the guidance period, those that are sound will continue as usual, and those with disputes will be re-assigned personnel for guidance. The appointment of new commissioners will be implemented only after the establishment of the new Provincial Government. (May 28th)

Murder and Robbery Case in Qingdao 51

Two Shop Assistants of Dejucheng Money Shop Shot Dead

More Than 1,100 Yuan in Banknotes Stolen

Qingdao Correspondence: At 8:30 p.m. on the 27th, two robbers, both in their twenties, wearing blue short jackets and top hats, suddenly entered the Dejucheng Money Shop in Quanshang Market on Market Road 3 while the accounts were being settled. They closed the door and said they wanted to exchange money. Then, they took out pistols and ordered shop assistants Wang Zhizuo and Ma Xijun to quickly go up to the top bunk. Ma then jumped out of the window and shouted. Hearing the warning, the robbers shot Ma in the abdomen. At that time, shopkeeper Ma Xihe was calling at the door outside. The robbers opened the door and shot and killed the shopkeeper Ma, one shot to the head, two shots to the abdomen, and one shot to the left hand, for a total of four wounds. At the same time, they snatched 1,110 yuan in silver dollars from the drawer and fled. After hearing the gunshots, the police on Market Road 3 rushed to the scene to investigate. Seeing that a murder had occurred, they immediately blew the whistle to warn and reported to the branch. The patrol officer of the branch led the police to the scene, but the robbers had already fled. A search was conducted in all directions, but no trace was found. The case was immediately reported to the branch bureau and then to the general bureau. The injured Ma Xi was sent to Qingdao Hospital for treatment and died in the hospital at 11:15 p.m. That night, Wu Tingzhang, the prosecutor of the local court, arrived to examine the body and prepare the coffin. The Public Security Bureau has ordered its subordinates to conduct a thorough investigation and strive to solve the case. Market Road 3 is a prosperous street in Qingdao City. Such a serious case of murder and robbery occurred in the evening, and local security suddenly felt terrorized. (May 28th)

Disaster Situation in Shaanxi and Recent News on Disaster Relief 52

More Than 60,000 People Died in Qian County

Zhu Qinglan Transports Rice to Lingbao

The disaster situation in Shaanxi Province is becoming more and more serious. The following is a quick telegram report from the Shaanxi Disaster Information Agency on the current situation and the disaster relief efforts of Zhu Qinglan and others. We hope philanthropists will pay attention to it.

(1) Qian County in Shaanxi Province is located on a plateau and has no land for irrigation. Last autumn, there was no harvest, and summer wheat has not yet been planted. The entire territory originally had a population of 169,498, and 61,634 have died. Four-tenths have demolished houses and sold them. There are households without any relatives in every village. There are nearly thirty villages with no human habitation. There have been three rains this year, and weeds grow everywhere on the wasteland. Many disaster victims who dig up weeds to prolong their lives develop swelling and die. No one buries them, resulting in the spread of epidemics. People are dying from starvation and epidemics. Although the Xiaohui Learning Society of Beiping has come to the county twice to distribute relief and has set up soup kitchens and shelters, it is a drop in the bucket, and only one percent is saved. Seeing the desolate scene, one's hair stands on end. The Shaanxi Disaster Information Agency bows in ashes.

(2) Philanthropist Zhu Qinglan left Xi'an early in the morning and returned east to transport seeds. He arrived in Zhengzhou on the 22nd and telegraphed Liu Yufen, Chairman of the Shaanxi Provincial Government, and Deng Changyao, Chairman of the Relief Committee, saying that 3,000 bags of corn seeds would arrive in Lingbao on the 24th. Please find a way to hire cars to transport them so that they can be delivered quickly. After receiving the telegram, Chairman Liu immediately sent Deputy Adjutant Ma and Mayor Yang to prepare cars. On the 23rd and 24th, the two chairmen, Liu and Deng, convened a meeting in the province with the managers of the Automobile Administration Bureau and more than 20 automobile companies to discuss the plan. The personnel of the automobile companies were grateful for the enthusiasm of Zhu and the provincial authorities in disaster relief and were willing to assist with all their strength. They jointly decided on several points: (1) The seed transportation fee will be reduced by half, 6 yuan per bag. (2) Cars will depart for transportation from the 1st. (3) Please allocate a car and a passport from the provincial government. (4) The number of bags transported by each car company will be registered on the passport each time. After the transportation is completed, the passport will be returned and a completed transportation license will be issued. (5) No matter whether it is a public or commercial car company, if there is no completed transportation license to carry passengers and goods, the car will be detained and not allowed to pass. (6) The amount of grain transported will be calculated according to the car's load. A one-ton car can transport 40 bags (transported in four trips), and a ton and a half car can transport 60 bags. It is expected that the transportation can be completed in about 10 days. On the 18th, the Chang'an Relief Sub-Committee of the Provincial Relief Committee sent personnel to assist in distributing the passports and transportation fees to each car company clearly overnight, and they set off the next morning. In addition, Mr. Shang Yunting and Zhang Huanhai, the representatives of Zhu in Xi'an, also sent a letter on the 23rd to the China Foreign Famine Relief Committee, the Red Cross Society, the Jisheng Sub-Committee, the Red Swastika Society, and other charitable organizations to discuss the seed distribution plan. It was decided to distribute seeds to the fifteen counties with severe disasters: Liquan, Pucheng, Sanyuan, Gaoling, Weinan, Mei County, Chang'an, Fufeng, Qishan, Jingyang, Qian County, Xingping, Zhouzhi, Xianyang, and Lintong. The Shaanxi Disaster Information Agency bows on the 1st.

(3) The Beijing China Foreign Famine Relief Committee, in view of the extraordinarily serious disaster situation in Shaanxi, has specially sent Arlington to Shaanxi to investigate the past disaster situation and survey the current disaster situation. Arlington has arrived in Yu H in the province. Although he is 72 years old, he is still energetic. He has been in China for more than 50 years and has assisted Li Hongzhang and Zhang Zhidong in handling confidential matters for many years. He has held important positions in the Ministry of Transportation of our country. In recent days, he has completed the investigation of the disaster situation in the vicinity of the provincial capital. He took a car to Xianyang, Xingping, Liquan, and other counties in the west of the province to conduct an on-site survey of the disaster situation early in the morning. In addition, Zhang Huanhai, Zhu Qinglan's representative in Shaanxi, also set off early in the morning to inspect disasters and provide relief in Liquan and Fufeng counties. In addition, Zhang Xianqing of the Shanghai Jisheng General Assembly went to Wugong to distribute emergency relief and seeds. The Shaanxi Disaster Information Agency bows on the 25th.

Liu Manqing Arrives in Lhasa to Investigate Border Affairs 53

According to news from Xikang, Ms. Liu Manqing, a secretary of the National Government, who was dispatched to Tibet for investigation last year, started her journey last year. When she traveled to a place 200 miles away from Ba'an via Ba'an, she was stopped by Tibetan bandits. After several negotiations, she was finally allowed to pass. She arrived in Lhasa on April 12. The Dalai Lama expressed his great welcome. It is heard that Ms. Liu will also go to the eastern entrance of the Himalayas to investigate the details of Nepal's invasion of Tibet. It is a groundbreaking move for a weak woman to go to the extreme border and work hard for the country.

Continued News on the Turmoil in the Russian Far East 54

Official Detectives Investigate Counter-Revolutionaries in All Directions

Anti-Soviet Groups Concentrate on the Suchang Coal Mine

Harbin Correspondence: Turmoil has occurred in the coastal region of Russia. According to Russian sources here, about several thousand anti-Soviet troops have gathered in the Ivanov and Mengnaisi areas. They have now invaded the Lazodori and Yefukanyika stations. The Soviet Russian political authorities are now secretly dispatching spies in all directions to investigate the inside information of the anti-Soviet group and its external methods. On May 18, the anti-Soviet group robbed the Soviet Russian garrison headquarters' supply team of bread and other foods in large quantities near Lazodori. Small anti-Soviet groups have also been found near Shatucheng, Woxingcheng, and Weibu. Therefore, the Weibu area is extremely tense. The Soviet Russian authorities have now implemented martial law in the port and its vicinity. According to the Soviet Russian Das Telegraph Agency, the passenger and freight cars attached to the locomotive No. 80 on the Ussuri Road derailed suddenly near the station of Kudolsk, resulting in many deaths and injuries. It is heard that the reason was that the anti-Soviet group secretly destroyed the railway. The anti-Soviet group of about 100 people in the area are moving in and out of the small mountains and forests. Nearby farmers have expressed their welcome and supplied them with matches and food. The Suchang Coal Mine, the largest in the Far East, has almost completely stopped working. Although the Red Army sent to suppress the anti-Soviet group drove out a part of it, recently anti-Soviet groups in [Siergeyev], [Frolokov], [Kekagongka] and other places may concentrate on Suchang as a base in the near future. In the [Right-wing Suke] and [Ima Alanulno] areas of the coastal region, although the Red Army is suppressing them, half of them were surrounded and killed by the anti-Soviet group, and half surrendered to the anti-Soviet group. In addition, farmers and workers in the northern Xiang area of ​​Ussuri Railway also rose up to riot against the Soviet Russian authorities. Although it did not succeed, they were always rising up, and the momentum was very large. As for the military weapons used, most of them were knives, axes, and guns seized from the Red Army. Judging from the current situation, it is feared that the Soviet authorities will not be able to clean it up easily for a while. (May 25th)

A Letter of Blood and Tears from All Chinese Merchants Living in Mongolia 55

(Continued)

Chinese merchants in Mongolia are unable to bear the heavy taxes and duties. Recently, some businesses have reported that they are closing down. The Mongolian authorities have stated that if they report that they are closing down, they will not be allowed to remit money when the Far Eastern Bank resumes business, even if the Chinese and Mongolian governments have a proper solution, they will not be allowed to operate again. Some businesses have no way to raise money for special taxes and duties, so they beg the Mongolian authorities to allow them to pay the taxes and duties in kind. The Mongolian authorities immediately accused the businesses of deliberately violating their regulations, confiscated all the goods of the businesses, and ordered the merchants to leave the country quickly. The types and amounts of taxes and duties are briefly recorded below. Silk fabrics, tobacco, and cosmetics are taxed at 30 per cent of their value. Leather goods, magnetic wooden utensils are taxed at 15 per cent of their value. Copper, iron, tin, and sugar are taxed at 16 per cent of their value. Cotton fabrics, paper, and all kinds of coarse goods are taxed at 6 per cent of their value. For leather goods leaving the country, fine leather goods are taxed at 30 per cent of their value, and coarse leather goods are taxed at 15 per cent of their value. The tax form fee is 1.05 yuan per form. The tax bureau weighing fee is 3 cents per 100 catties. The tax bureau care fee is 1.2 cents per 100 catties per day. The entrance and exit tax bureau door fee is 50 cents per item. The tax bureau unpacking fee is 20 cents per item. The transportation bureau transportation fee is 1.4 yuan per 100 catties. The passport fee is 80 yuan per person per year, plus a police donation of 5 yuan. The travel permit fee is 9 yuan per person per month. The salary donation is 120 yuan per year for the person in charge of the business, and 30 yuan per year for the staff. The business license donation is divided into eight grades: the special grade is not limited to the number of people, and is 9,000 yuan per year; the first grade is not limited to the number of people, and is 4,500 yuan per year; the second grade is not limited to the number of people, and is 2,500 yuan per year; the third grade is limited to 12 people, and is 1,500 yuan per year; the fourth grade is limited to 8 people, and is 1,000 yuan per year; the fifth grade is limited to 6 people, and is 500 yuan per year; the sixth grade is limited to 4 people, and is 250 yuan per year; the seventh grade is limited to 2 people, and is 150 yuan per year. The capital donation is 25 yuan per 1,000 yuan. The flow donation is 12 per cent per year. The actual number is multiplied by three or five times, and the donation bureau can estimate the increase at will. The bonus donation is 50 per cent per year. Regardless of whether there is any surplus profit, the bonus of 150 yuan per 1,000 yuan is estimated according to the amount of flow. The doorplate donation is divided into eight grades: the special grade is 1,200 yuan per year; the first grade is 800 yuan per year; the second grade is 600 yuan per year; the third grade is 300 yuan per year; the fourth grade is 200 yuan per year; the fifth grade is 150 yuan per year; the sixth grade is 100 yuan per year; the seventh grade is 80 yuan per year. The land foundation donation is divided into three grades: the first grade is 1.8 cents per step per year; the second grade is 1.4 cents per step per year; the third grade is 1 cent per step per year. The house donation is calculated by adding twice the actual price, and is 60 yuan per 1,000 yuan per year. In addition, the donation for people living in the house is 15 yuan per room per year, the donation for storage rooms is 30 yuan per room per year, and the donation for kitchens is 5 yuan per room per year. The degree of donation is 3 yuan per pair for rulers. The large scale is 30 yuan per year, and the small scale is 8 yuan per year. The tobacco license donation is 120 yuan per year for all kinds of tobacco sold in whole, and 80 yuan for those sold in retail. To sum up, we Chinese people in Outer Mongolia have long been unbearable under the political and economic aggression of the red imperialism. However, the property and goods of the Mongolian business trip are still as high as 540 million yuan, according to a reliable survey. They are all blocked and cannot be cleaned up. They can only die. In addition to the direct and indirect losses suffered by Mongolian businesses and northwestern ports, and there will be no survivors, the number of Chinese and foreign goods exported to the outside of the country from Tianjin and Tianjin in the past was very large. Now, once it is stopped, Tianjin and Tianjin businesses will also suffer a major blow. Although there is no clear survey of tax revenue, the sharp reduction in imports and exports will inevitably have a major impact on revenue. In general, Outer Mongolia is a large sales market for our country's goods and a large source of money in the Northwest. Its relationship with our prosperity and decline is truly not superficial. Our Mongolian merchants are in dire straits and cannot live or die. There is no response to crying out to the heavens, and no response to calling out to the earth. We can only plead with patriotic and people-saving people from all walks of life to speak out in unison and urge the authorities to quickly take measures to provide relief, so as to protect the country's territory and relieve the people's suffering. China is fortunate, all northwestern ports are fortunate, and all Mongolian merchants are fortunate. Sincerely, all overseas Chinese merchants in Mongolia,

Wuxi 59

Yan Guangmao's Silk Cocoon Firm Catches Fire: The silk cocoon firms in the four villages of this county have successively stopped weighing. It is learned that Yan Guangmao's silk cocoon firm in the Wumu area of Henglin, which borders Wuxi and Wu, was rented this year by Ding Rulin's son Xianglong, a silk merchant from Shanghai. It opened for six days and collected more than 1,000 loads of fresh cocoons. Every day, it was baked, packaged, and transported back to Shanghai for delivery. Unexpectedly, on the day of closing, a fire alarm was suddenly reported in the dry cocoon room. After the workers in the firm drew water to extinguish the fire, it was extinguished shortly. It is estimated that a number of loads of dry cocoons were burned. The firm had fire insurance of 40,000 taels. After the incident, it immediately reported to the Shanghai headquarters to send someone to inspect and claim compensation for the loss. The result is unknown.

A Pig Boat in Baitangwei Meets Robbers: Zhang Yuxiu, a native of Yanqiao in the northern township of this county, has always been engaged in the business of transporting piglets. Recently, he undertook to transport 75 strong pigs from Yongmao Pig Farm in Daoshiqiao, Taixing County, Jiangbei, to Hengtai Pig Farm in Qimen, Suzhou for delivery. Unexpectedly, at about 10:00 p.m. the night before, when the boat was passing through Baitangwei in our county, it was suddenly encountered by a boat. Nine robbers jumped out, each holding a handgun, flashlight, and other weapons, and ordered the boat to stop. They jumped onto the pig boat and searched extensively. After half an hour, they carried the stolen goods across the boat and drove away quickly. Boatman Zhang Yuxiu did not report to the county because the loss was still small.

A Monk Murders a Nun for Money: In the 395th map area of Nanyan City (11th District) in this county, there is a Shuiyue Nunnery. It was learned by Wang Delin, a monk from a nearby temple. Police Unit Suppresses Bandits in Shazhou: Regarding the case of five men and women kidnapped from the home of Ma Yunbin, a traditional Chinese medicine practitioner in Baimao Estuary, Dongwu District, it is now known that Ma Yunbin, who was kidnapped, and his student Gu Rulong, were shot and killed during the military and police suppression. Purchase of Firearms Encountered Difficulties: For the sake of defending the locality, the county government had ordered firearms from the Yali Foreign Firm in Shanghai. It has recently been learned that these firearms will soon be shipped to Shanghai. The county specially commissioned Lu Baozhong, the chief inspector of the Public Security Bureau, and Wu Xinheng, the head of District 1, to take documents to Shanghai to pick them up. Unexpectedly, when the firearms passed through the Jianghai Customs by ship, they were not allowed to be transported ashore because they only had a provincial government passport and not a national government passport. The ship was anchored on the river bank at Jianghai Customs, and the crew claimed that the ship would lose 3,000 taels per day of delay. If the problem was not resolved, the firearms would be thrown into the sea. The Wujin County government's representatives were also waiting in Shanghai because Changzhou had also ordered hundreds of rifles from the same foreign firm. It is now known that Lu and Wu have negotiated with the representatives from Changzhou and requested the ship to stay for 24 hours. The loss of 3,000 taels will be borne by this county and Wujin. At the same time, they entrusted the Songhu authorities to negotiate with Minister Song of the Ministry of Finance and asked Guo Di to rush to obtain the passport. All the firearms would be purchased by the Ministry of Finance. Although the deposit paid by this county can be refunded, the losses incurred in delaying the ship and in purchasing and selling the firearms are already substantial.

Magistrate Li immediately ordered the Public Security Bureau and the police team, together with the district branch bureau, to go to the destination yesterday morning and detain 20 suspects. They were taken to Shengang and interrogated by District Head Huang. Six people were found to be closely related and were immediately taken to the city. When the police team was unloading bullets on the street, a gun accidentally discharged and wounded four children. Ding Ganggen and Yin Youfu were the most seriously injured and were immediately taken to the Gospel Hospital in the city for treatment. Their injuries are not life-threatening.

Exploiting the Labor Dispute Remains Difficult to Resolve: Exploiting the rice subsidy turmoil in the yarn factory led to a strike. Zhong Jianhui, a member of the county party headquarters, mediated and signed the conditions. The Public Security Bureau released the detained suspects, Shen Zhangbao and 15 others, and only detained the representatives Ren Ruisheng and Li Jinsheng, who would be released after work resumed. Yesterday morning, when the workers were about to go to work at the factory, the iron gate was tightly closed. Manager Wang Yiyun suddenly regretted his previous agreement, saying that the conditions had to be resolved by the board of directors because the factory's business had also been poor recently, resulting in heavy losses. The workers then returned home. Member Zhong contacted the factory again, but the company's attitude was firm. Member Zhong immediately telegraphed the provincial party headquarters for instructions. The labor dispute remains difficult to resolve. The Public Security Bureau has not released the detained representatives Ren Ruisheng and others.

Security Chief Detained Pending Trial: Chen Songshan, the head of the Deshun Township security force, was accused by Shi Xilin, the younger brother of Shi Daguan, of arbitrarily arresting people, inflicting private torture resulting in injuries, and moving the body after death to make it appear as if he had committed suicide by hanging. After Magistrate Li approved the indictment, he summoned Chief Chen and security guard Zhang Guowei on the 31st. Chen was placed under guard, and Zhang was detained. The trial is scheduled to begin in three days.

Yangzhou 64

Recent Financial Problems in the Education Sector: The education sector in Jiangdu has been facing difficulties for the past six months due to years of famine and frequent changes of directors, resulting in accumulated arrears of educational funds for four or five months. After the new director, Chen Lanfang, took office, he was deeply concerned about the extreme hardship of his colleagues in the education sector. As a first step, he devised various methods to raise funds. Since taking office on the 16th of this month, he had raised and distributed funds for one and a half months (totaling more than 27,000 yuan) by yesterday (30th), which has slightly stabilized morale. It is now heard that Director Chen plans to raise funds for another two months before the summer vacation. Whether or not he can fulfill this wish is still unknown.

Chamber of Commerce Accused of Colluding with Bandits - Ordered to Investigate: Tao Xuezhong, the leader of the Xiannvmiao Chamber of Commerce team in the county, was accused of colluding with bandits and defecting to the North. Li, the director of the Provincial Security Department, instructed the 133rd Brigade stationed in Yangzhou to send a platoon of soldiers to search Tao's residence and intended to bring Tao to the city to be interrogated by the province. However, the local merchants believed that Chief Tao would never do such a thing. Guan Mengting, the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, also issued a letter of guarantee and sent it to the team to reinstate its mandate. Therefore, the chief was spared the loss of freedom.

Reduction in Slaughter Tax for Bidding: The slaughter tax in Jiangdu County was increased, resulting in no one bidding. The county submitted a request to the Provincial Education Funding Management Office for instructions. An order was received approving a reduction of five percent from the original amount (the original amount was 24,120 yuan) and rescheduling the bidding for June 15, with a new public announcement.

Two Districts Borrow Grain for Poverty Relief: The ninth and tenth districts of Jiangdu County plan to allocate 6,000 yuan of accumulated grain (to be returned after the autumn harvest) to provide relief loans to alleviate poverty. The county has approved this plan. The county government, based on the request from the districts, ordered the Grain Storage Management Committee to negotiate the loan methods directly with the districts and report on the implementation.

Cancellation of Custody of Two Pawnshop Redemption Funds: Although the labor dispute at the Changling Pawnshop had been resolved earlier, all the redemption funds had been placed under the custody of county government official Ling Han and deposited in the Dechun Huichang Yong Pawnshops. It is now known that after the pawnshop dispute was resolved, the custody of the redemption funds was canceled. After repeated requests, instructions have now been received from the Provincial Department of Construction and approved. Magistrate Chen has ordered Commissioner Ling, the Changling, Yuanhe pawnshops, and the pawnshops to be informed.

Gaoyou 65

Sudden Martial Law in This County: For some unknown reason, the county government of this county suddenly issued a special martial law order this afternoon. The first squadron of police, armed with live ammunition, was on alert in front of the county government's auditorium. The market was temporarily in a state of panic, traffic was cut off, and pedestrians were prohibited from traveling. At the same time, an urgent telegram was sent to the Provincial Department of Civil Affairs to report the martial law situation.

Director Zhou Proven to Have No Opium Addiction: Zhou Zhendong, the director of the Public Security Bureau of this county, was previously accused of smoking opium by citizens Wang Bingbi and others in a complaint to the Department of Civil Affairs. Zhou, unwilling to be examined in this county, applied for leave from the county government and went to the province for examination. The department designated the Provincial Hospital and sent personnel to supervise the examination for a week. He was found to have no opium addiction. He has now completed his leave and returned to Gaoyou to resume his duties.

Nanjing 66

Zhang Fuqing and Others File Charges Against Meng Enyuan: Meng Enyuan, the former military governor of Jilin, was charged with illegally occupying the Harbin Electric Light Company and selling it to the Jilin Yongheng Official Bank for 1.94 million yuan. At that time, various newspapers published articles stating that Meng had improper behavior. Citizens Liu Zhongshu and others jointly requested the provincial government to confiscate the Electric Light Company and return it to the public. Meng settled the matter with money. Shareholders Kong Xianzhang also filed charges with the Ministry of Industry and Commerce of the National Government to investigate. It has now been learned that Zhang Fuqing, a third-party creditor, has joined the lawsuit and filed charges with the National Government against Meng for various illegal acts during his tenure. Citizens He Jingyang and others have also accused Meng of six major crimes and requested the National Government to order the governor of Jilin Province to arrest Meng and escort him to Beijing for trial.

Jiaxing 67

Provincial Order Exempts Hotel Registration Books from Stamp Tax: Hotels in Jiaxing are equipped with registration books for filling in information about guests. Penalties often occur because stamp duty is not paid. Recently, the Gaosheng Hotel in Dongmen was found by an investigator from the Stamp Tax Bureau to have failed to affix stamps to the guest registration book, which was deemed to be a violation of the stamp duty regulations. The book was taken to the bureau and transferred to the County Public Security Bureau for punishment. The hotel refused to accept the judgment and reported it to the Chengdong Commercial Association. After receiving the report, the association stated that the registration book only contained information such as the guest's age, appearance, origin, and destination for the Public Security Bureau's inspection. It was not related to trade accounts or commercial books, and it was doubtful that stamp duty should be required. It jointly telegraphed the Provincial Stamp Tax Bureau, requesting an explanation on behalf of the various commercial associations in Beidajie and Beimenwai. A telegram was received in reply, stating that the guest registration book specifically prepared by the hotel for the Public Security Bureau's inspection was not related to trade and should be exempt from stamp duty. After receiving the telegram, the association notified the County Public Security Bureau and the Jiaxing Stamp Tax Sub-Bureau yesterday.

Jiashan 68

County Government Investigates Brick Factory's Mud Excavation Case: Pingyao Town has always been a place for the production of bricks and tiles, with a large volume of external sales each year. Several years ago, merchants from Shanghai pooled funds in the town to open companies such as Taishan, Huaxin, and Shantai Taoxin, specializing in Western tiles, which were transported and sold to Shanghai and other places. The mud used was obtained from the nearby fields. Citizens of the town filed a complaint with the provincial government, accusing the companies of excavating field mud, damaging farmland, and violating prohibitions. The provincial government instructed the county to transfer the case to the Public Security Bureau, which sent personnel to conduct an on-site investigation on separate days and submit a factual report.

Relocation of the Nursery to the City: The Shenxianggong Nursery outside the East Gate of the city was too small. The County Relief Institute selected the old site of the Dianye Guild Hall in Huayuan Alley in the city and rebuilt it. The relocation was carried out on the day before yesterday.

Chinese Medicine Association Re-elects Executive and Supervisory Committees: The Jiashan Chinese Medicine Association convened its second general assembly yesterday. Shen Jiren chaired the meeting and discussed matters for further action. The election was then held. The results were as follows: Executive Committee members: Shen Jiren, Chen Changnian, Zhang Jixuan, Yao Jingming, Xu Shinian, Sheng Yucheng, Ding Feiting, Zhang Jinwen, Gu Bolong. Supervisory Committee members: Sun Fengling, Qian Weiru, Xu Qinpu.

Kidnapping Case in Shi Jia Bang, Gan Yao: Last night, more than 20 bandits broke into the home of Lu Mengqiao, a farmer from another province, in Shi Jia Bang, Gan Yao Township. Lu, his son, and his nephew Afu were all kidnapped, and a large sum of money was demanded for their release.

Four Bandits Captured, Currently Under Official Interrogation: The Seventh Water Police Team in Gan Yao captured four bandits from Dongxiang in the Xitang District last night. They are currently under strict interrogation. It is said that one of the monks who escaped has confessed to many accomplices.

Pinghu 69

Director of the Sports Field Dismissed: Fang County Magistrate recently issued an order to dismiss Wang Mengxiong from his position as director of the Public Sports Field in Zhapu, as he was wanted by the County Government and Water and Land Police for a case. Liu Dihua, the director of the Public Education Museum, was ordered to take over the position, and a qualified person will be selected to fill it.

Zhang Yousong Rescued from Dayun Temple by the Hangzhou Security Team: After Zhang Yousong was kidnapped by bandits, there was no news of him. It has now been learned that 11 of the kidnappers have been captured by the Security Team in Hangzhou, and Zhang has also been rescued. After learning the news, Zhang's family is preparing funds to go to Hangzhou to reward the team and bring Yousong home.

Military Troops Search Bandit Hideouts: Zhao, the battalion commander of the Second Battalion of the Seventh Regiment of the Provincial Security Team, led the entire Sixth Company on special missions, traveling by the Shangwu shallow-water patrol ship and the Gongbei, Xin Jiahai, and Ningxin ships. They arrived in Xin from Ping on the morning of the 29th at 1:00 AM. The Fifth Company stationed in Xincang was also transferred to join the Sixth Company, proceeding from Yaqian. The battalion commander personally led the Fourth Company on special missions, taking the route through Xinmiao, searching and advancing in two directions to suppress bandits. They met at Wanchun Bridge in the Langxia District of Jinshan. A small teahouse there was identified as a bandit organization. They surrounded and arrested those inside, capturing more than 20 people, including tea drinkers. Several bandits were also captured in nearby areas and at Xiangxian Nunnery in the northwest of Qianjiawei. A pistol was confiscated. A total of 34 people were arrested in this operation. The prisoners were escorted back to Xin after noon. Zhao, the battalion commander, also brought Cao Rongsheng, a thief who had confessed, to the Baiyang Court at the East Market at 2:00 PM and executed him by shooting as a warning to the public. Zhao then led the special missions of the Fourth Company back to Ping with the prisoners. The Sixth Company and the Twelfth Company remained stationed in Xincang.

Ningbo 70

Director of the Zhenhai Stamp Tax Bureau Resigns: Since taking office, Bao Zhen, the director of the Zhenhai Stamp Tax Bureau, has maintained a harmonious relationship with the business community. He has now resigned from his position due to certain reasons, which has been approved by the provincial bureau. A new director, Zou, has been appointed to take over. Zou has arrived in office and is scheduled to be formally sworn in on June 5.

Two Violent Robbers on Wupoling: Zhang Deli, from Sheng County, was returning home from Cao'e at 3:00 PM the day before yesterday. While passing through Wupoling in Zhangjiabu, two fierce-looking bandits suddenly jumped out from between the trees, each wielding a machete. They blocked Zhang's path, searched him, and robbed him of three silver dollars, five yuan in banknotes, and eight jiao in small coins. After getting the money, the bandits fled towards the plains.

Shaoxing 71

Tragic Incident of Bandits Robbing a Prisoner: A tragic incident of bandits robbing a prisoner occurred in Gaobu, Shaoxing, on the night of the 30th. The details are as follows: The prisoner, named Qian Yichen, was being escorted from Hangzhou to Sheng County. The Shaoxing Public Security Bureau assigned patrol team soldiers Xie Guitang and Zhou Genyuan to take the late-night boat to Sheng from Haoba. When they approached Gaobu, it was already late at night. Two bandits suddenly jumped out inside the boat, each wielding a wooden-sheathed gun. They ordered Xie Guitang to release the prisoner. When he hesitated, the bandits opened fire. Xie Guitang was shot twice in the abdomen and once in the leg. He immediately fell to the ground in a pool of blood. The bandits then ordered the boatman to dock and instructed Zhou Genyuan to lead the way west. The boat carried the wounded soldier to Gaobu and reported it to the Public Security Branch Bureau. The news was relayed to the city by telephone. The Public Security Bureau immediately sent a team of soldiers to Gaobu to pursue the bandits. The wounded soldier was sent to the city for treatment overnight, but he died en route due to his serious injuries. The soldiers dispatched from the city encountered the bandits and the robbed prisoner on the narrow road in front of the bus station outside the Wuyun Gate. They ordered them to stop, but the bandits opened fire, wounding the team soldier Wang Jinsheng in the left foot. The two bandits and the prisoner fled north. When the Public Security Bureau subsequently sent an inspector along with various police chiefs and detectives to arrest them, the bandits had already fled far away.

Fire at Shimenkan, Wuwuqiao, Inside the City: A fire broke out at the home of a certain family in Shimenkan, Wuwuqiao, inside the city, at midnight on the 30th. It is estimated that five or six dozen houses belonging to the Qianshaotang maternity clinic and the Wangtongshun foil shop were burned down.

Shangyu 72

Two Deserters Drown: Six deserters from a certain regiment stationed in Wufu were pursued and arrested by local military police on the afternoon of the 25th. Four escaped into the water, and two were captured. On the 29th and 30th, the county government received reports from the local police in the first district that two floating bodies had been discovered in Tianda Pond. Zhu Chengyuan went to examine the bodies and confirmed that they were the deserters who had drowned after jumping into the pond. He ordered that coffins be prepared for burial. It is also reported that two escaped soldiers are hiding in the mountains near Lianghu Town in the fourth district. One of them is carrying a pistol and has been demanding food and lodging from homes in the mountains. They are elusive, making it difficult to track their whereabouts.

Incoming Letter L [

Letter from Yan Juezhi et al., Wuxi 73

Dear Sir, We read with astonishment the article titled "Libidinous Scoundrel Rapes Young Girl" in the Wuxi correspondence section of your newspaper on the 23rd of this month. Our establishments are located directly opposite and next to (Yongfengshun) Fruit Store. We did not witness any such rape incident occurring on that day. Moreover, the temple is the busiest commercial area in our city, with shops lining the streets and pedestrians constantly passing by throughout the night. Furthermore, our establishments were not yet closed at 9:00 PM. It is obvious to all that the store clerk, You Ruichang, could not have tricked and raped the girl. The details in your newspaper's article are likely based on mistaken rumors. As this matter concerns local customs and the reputation of the store, we, as close neighbors, feel compelled to write this letter on their behalf, even if it seems presumptuous. We hope that you will publish our letter to dispel any doubts. We are grateful. Yan Juezhi, Zhang Zheng, Li Shuping, Zhu Muzhou, Dai Shaohong, May 31.

Letter from Zhang Shaoqin, Dingfengyong Silk Factory, Zhenjiang 74

Yesterday, I read with astonishment the article titled "Another Dispute at Dingfengyong Silk Factory" in the Zhenjiang News section of your newspaper. The leader of the reeler worker's small group at the former Qinyi Silk Factory, Xu Erniang, was not hired by our factory because of her poor skills when we began operations. When Xu was not hired, Wang Siso immediately declared that if Xu wasn't working, everyone would stop working together, instigating a strike. Fortunately, most of the workers did not follow her lead and continued to work. After mediation by the Zhenjiang County Workers' Restructuring Committee, it was requested that she be tried out, which has already been done. Since our factory began operations on May 26 of this year, no strike has occurred. The article in your newspaper is likely based on mistaken rumors. As this matter concerns labor unrest, it is inappropriate to allow it to cause confusion. I am writing this quick letter to correct the record. I hope that it will be published in the Incoming Letters section. I would be grateful. Sincerely, Zhang Shaoqin, Manager of Dingfengyong Silk Factory, 19, 5, 31.

Shigemitsu Suspends Return to His Country 77

Shigemitsu Aoi, the Japanese Chargé d'Affaires in China, was previously summoned back to his country by the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs to consult on future steps in negotiations with China and the issue of Ambassador Obata's visit to China. The date of Mr. Shigemitsu's departure had been postponed repeatedly. It was later set for yesterday on the Chichibu Maru. Unexpectedly, the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs suddenly instructed Shigemitsu to suspend his return to his country. Therefore, Shigemitsu was unable to leave yesterday. Whether Shigemitsu will still return to Tokyo in the future is also uncertain. According to the general observation of the Japanese, it is believed that Shigemitsu's suspension of his return to his country is related to the political situation in China.

The Preparatory Committee for Commercial Consolidation Prepares to Convene a Delegates' Congress 78

Formal Establishment of the Shanghai Special City Chamber of Commerce

The Preparatory Committee for Commercial Consolidation, having resolved through a plenary committee meeting, has scheduled a city-wide delegates' congress for June 21st to formally establish the Shanghai Special City Chamber of Commerce. Yesterday, it submitted reports to the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, and applied for permission from the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs. The original text stated that the powers stipulated in Article 3 of the organizational outline of our committee are: (1) Registering members of the former Shanghai Merchants' Association, Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, Zhabei Chamber of Commerce, and Nanshi Chamber of Commerce; (2) Drafting regulations for a unified organization in accordance with laws and regulations; (3) Preparing all organizational procedures for a unified organization. Currently, the first item, the registration procedure, has already been completed. The second item, the regulations of the Shanghai Special City Chamber of Commerce, has also been drafted and submitted to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce by the Bureau of Social Affairs for approval. We proceeded according to the amendments of the Bureau of Social Affairs and, following the 51st executive meeting of our committee, amended them in accordance with the approved instructions. As for the third item, among the registered merchant organizations, 138 trade associations have been reorganized under the guidance of our committee, and 23 trade associations have been merged under the guidance of our committee. Among these 138 trade associations, 20 have completed reorganization. However, according to Article 14 of the Law on Industrial and Commercial Associations promulgated by the National Government on August 17, 1929, [existing industrial and commercial associations prior to the implementation of this law, regardless of whether they are called public offices, guilds, or other names, whose aims are in accordance with the provisions of this law, shall be regarded as industrial and commercial associations established in accordance with this law, and shall be reorganized in accordance with this law within one year after its implementation]. The mission undertaken by our committee is to guide the local merchant organizations in accordance with laws and regulations. The Law on Industrial and Commercial Associations clearly stipulates that the time limit for reorganization is one year. Although our committee urges the trade associations to actively reorganize in accordance with the law, the time limit for reorganization granted by the law cannot be changed. Furthermore, the Law on Industrial and Commercial Associations also clearly stipulates that all those whose aims are in accordance with the provisions of Article 2 of this law shall be regarded as industrial and commercial associations established in accordance with this law. Therefore, within the scope of this city, the 138 trade associations reorganized under the guidance of our committee, although some have not yet completed reorganization in fact, their legal status has been completely determined. Furthermore, Article 12 of our committee's organizational outline stipulates that the Shanghai Commercial Consolidation Committee shall apply the service rules of the various levels of mass organization consolidation committees passed by the 150th executive meeting of the Central Committee in June 1928. Article 7 of those rules stipulates that when more than one-third of the lower-level organizations under the jurisdiction of the Consolidation Committee of Mass Organizations of each special city or county-level city have completed consolidation, they should report to the Party Headquarters of each special city or county-level city to send people to inspect. If it is deemed that a delegates' congress of mass organizations of the entire province (special city) or county (city) can be convened, the delegates' congress of the entire province (special city) or county (city) may be convened immediately. Currently, there are a total of 161 trade associations in this city that have been reorganized and merged under the guidance of our committee in accordance with the law. Among these 161 trade associations, 138 trade associations have been legally determined to be able to exercise their functions, which greatly exceeds the one-third requirement. Now, in order to complete the task of [establishing the organization of a unified group] stipulated in Article 15 of our committee's organizational outline, all organizational procedures for preparing a unified group are being actively carried out, and convening a delegates' congress of trade associations is a particularly important procedure for preparing a unified group. After considering the situation, it is urgently necessary to stipulate a date and hold it as soon as possible. Therefore, at the 13th plenary meeting of our committee on the 22nd of this month, it was resolved to convene a delegates' congress of trade associations in this city on June 21st, and to state the reasons in advance and apply for permission from the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Bureau of Social Affairs. As for the remaining organizations that have been merged under the guidance of our committee in accordance with the law but have not yet been completed, it is proposed that the reorganization committee of the relevant trade organization exercise its powers on its behalf, and recommend delegates in accordance with the regulations to attend the meeting together. This is because the nature of the reorganization committee of each relevant organization is to exercise the former powers of each merged organization on behalf of it during the reorganization period, which is the same as our committee exercising the powers of the four former merchant organizations on behalf of it. Recommending delegates to attend the meeting is also within the scope of exercising powers on its behalf, and should not be restricted separately. All the reasons for requesting permission to convene a delegates' congress of trade associations in this city are hereby stated. In addition to sending separate letters, we hereby request your review and filing for public convenience.

Minutes of the Standing Committee Meeting of the Municipal Training Association 84

Ninth Meeting

The Mass Training Committee of the Shanghai Special City Executive Committee held its ninth standing committee meeting on May 30th, chaired by Mr. Chen Junyi. The meeting opened as scheduled. The following is an excerpt of the matters discussed: (1) The letter from the Commercial Consolidation Committee, stating the reasons for convening a delegates' congress of trade associations in this city as resolved by the plenary meeting, and requesting permission to convene the meeting. Resolved: Permission is granted to convene the meeting. (2) The report from the East District Yarn Factory Labor Consolidation Committee on the establishment process, expenditure arrears, and requesting review and compliance. Resolved: Investigate the case. (3) The letter from the Public Security Bureau, regarding Lin Xiaoshan's initiation of the Shanghai South Shipping Merchants' Union, and Xun Shizhe's accusations, which were found to be inconsistent. Inquire whether it should be dissolved immediately, and requesting a reply for verification. Resolved: The organization of the union is inconsistent and the Public Security Bureau should be requested to dissolve it. (4) The Secretariat forwarded the request from the General Labor Union, requesting the committee to jointly order all labor unions with the Bureau of Social Affairs to use the [May 1st] holiday wages as the Labor Hospital and Labor Education Fund. Resolved: The standing committee members will discuss with the Bureau of Social Affairs and then submit to the meeting for further review. Resolved: Proceed according to the proposed method. (6) The First District Party Headquarters requested the addition of members to the reorganization committee of the spice industry workers' union. Resolved: Approved. (7) The request from the Minsheng Yarn Factory Labor Union for the issuance of a license and a certificate of sound organization, and requesting review after examination. Resolved: Permission is granted to certify the sound organization. (8) The Sixth District Executive Committee requested instructions on whether the Law on the Handling of Labor-Capital Disputes can be applied to labor-capital disputes in companies and businesses. (9) The Commercial Consolidation Committee requested that newly organized trade organizations first issue a certificate from our committee and then apply to your committee for certification. Requested Mr. Tao to review and request for review. Resolved: Reply to the Commercial Consolidation Committee by letter. (10) The secretary of the South Goods Industry Workers' Union acted improperly. After investigation, it is proposed to dismiss him. Resolved: Passed, and Mr. Xu Qi is appointed to take over. (11) The letter from the Municipal Government, enclosing a copy of the revised charter of the Municipal Deliberation Committee on Rent Disputes, requesting verification and the street names of the representatives to be returned in advance. Resolved: Appoint Mr. Yang Qingyuan as the representative. (12) Mr. Tao submitted that the draft charter of the Shanghai Special City Chamber of Commerce submitted for review has been reviewed, with attached comments, and requesting for review. Resolved: Passed according to the review comments, and further discuss with the Bureau of Social Affairs. (Temporary motions) 1. Mr. Wu Kaixian submitted that the Shanghai Mass Organizations Overview and Historical Sketch Compilation Plan submitted for review has been completed, and is generally appropriate, and requesting for review. Resolved: Passed according to the review comments. 2. Supplementing the executive committee of the Quanxi He Yarn Factory Labor Union. Resolved: Supplement Chen Yurong, Wang Guiying, Li Jinhai, Ren Shoushan, Gu Changsheng, Li Jinjin, Gu Xianzong, Zhou Ziyang and other eight people as executive committee members, and Chen Dasheng, Liu Hanyong, Fang Zhenjia, Liu Congsheng, Li Zhendi, Zhang Lanying, Zhang Kouhan and other seven people as alternate executive committee members. 3. Ju Ganxin, etc., requested to order the human-powered vehicle merchant organizations in the concession and the north and south cities to handle educational undertakings in order to emphasize public welfare and maintain public sentiment. According to the investigation report, Ju Ganxin, etc., are indeed vehicle merchants, and the vehicle merchant association collects a large amount of donations every month. It would be beneficial to establish schools, and facilitation should be provided. Resolved: Approved.

Postal Unions Request the Abolition of the Document Clerk and Assistant Positions by Telegraph 85

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union and Postal Employees' Union quickly telegraphed (titles omitted)

Publicly Appraised, Our China Post, after more than thirty years of operation, relies on the strictness of regulations and the spirit of examination. Fortunately, in the dark environment, it has been able to cleanse the murky and eliminate the corrupt, and not be mixed with them. Unexpectedly, last month, the Postal Administration, outside of the personnel grades stipulated in the Postal Regulations approved and promulgated by the National Government, arbitrarily established the deformed system of assistant and document clerks, and without holding legal examinations, privately extended personal invitations to twelve people to serve as document clerks and three people to serve as assistants. The latter has a monthly salary of 500 yuan for one person and 350 yuan for two people, and there is a pre-determination to be appointed as deputy postmaster in two years. The former has a monthly salary starting at 160 yuan, increasing annually to 280 yuan. Upon close inspection of the resumes of the assistants, one once served as an engineer, one once served as a consul of a certain country, and only one once served as an attendant of the postal association. The members of the document clerks are even more complex. At most, they are ignorant of postal knowledge and perfunctory in their duties. Alas, the rewards that our postal service personnel cannot obtain after a lifetime of hard work, or after decades of service, are now safely enjoyed by these people in one fell swoop. What injustice is greater than this? In the long run, it will lead to bribery, and success will be achieved through bribery. The fortunate ones

Page 14

will be prominent, and the meritorious ones will be demoralized. Is the future of the postal service still worth asking about? Our Zeng and others, considering the difficulty of establishing the postal service, thoroughly oppose this system of document clerks and assistants that violates the teachings of the Premier and destroys the postal system. If there is a need for document and assistant affairs, the usual practice can be followed, and experienced personnel can be selected from among the senior staff to serve in order to be skilled. If this is not sufficient, legal examinations can be held in accordance with the regulations, and they can be assigned separately according to their existing grades. As for the twelve document clerks and assistants who have already been employed, since there is no basis in the postal regulations and they have not undergone legal examinations, their positions should be terminated. This opinion has already been submitted to the Central Party Headquarters, the various ministries and departments of the National Government, and the newly appointed Postmaster General Wei Yifu for verification. The entire staff of our association is panicked. For the sake of the Party, for the sake of the postal service, and for the sake of our 400 million compatriots, we dare not be lenient. We sincerely hope that compatriots from all walks of life will understand that the selfishness of a few people will result in harm to the development of the postal service, and may even affect the overall political situation. We must unite and fight together to support them. Then the central government and the officials of the national government, with their clear vision, will surely find a solution through revolutionary means, so that the postal system will be complete, corruption will disappear, and then the bright and brilliant postal service can be realized. We earnestly and painfully plead, and humbly request your consideration.

Guo Qingzhao Passed Away on May 30th 87

The Funeral Will Be Held at 10:00 AM Today

Guo Qingzhao, a member of the Kuomintang, was resented by the communists for his efforts to purify the party. On May 5, 1930, he was attacked by communist thugs on Beile Road in the French Concession, shot in the waist and spine, and sent to Guangci Hospital for treatment. However, because the spinal nerve system was severed by the bullet, the upper part of his body could eat, speak, and move normally after recovery, but the lower part of his body lost sensation, resulting in disability. In May of this year, he was admitted to the Fumin Hospital established by the Japanese on North Sichuan Road to undergo surgery to reconnect the nerve system. He underwent surgery at 3:00 PM on the 5/30 Memorial Day, and due to excessive bleeding, he passed away at 8:00 PM that night. The following is a brief account of Mr. Guo's life and circumstances:

A Brief Account of Mr. Guo's Life Mr. Guo, 25 years old, a native of Ninghai, Zhejiang Province, was a top student at Zhejiang Provincial Fourth Middle School. He worked in the manufacturing department of the Shanghai Commercial Press as a typesetter. In 1925, he witnessed the May 30th Massacre and was angered by the brutality of the imperialists. To seek a proper way out for the workers, he resolutely joined the Chinese Kuomintang as a member, firmly believing in the Three People's Principles and studying them in depth. He was fierce, ambitious, and courageous. In his spare time, he still went to Shanggong Youth Lizhi Association night school for supplementary education. He then secretly discovered that the communists had a plot to overthrow the Chinese Kuomintang, so he secretly formed loyal comrades to fight for the party. Then, in April 1927, he implemented the purification of the party. Mr. Guo was then the standing committee member of the 14th branch of the First District, so he took the lead in launching the movement, and all the communists who were hiding in the factory of the Commercial Press were cleared out. Therefore, he was deeply trusted by the Central Committee and served as a standing committee member of the Commercial Press Labor Union, the Minister of Agriculture and Labor of the First District Party Headquarters, the instructor of the Shanghai Labor Union Unity Committee, the Standing Committee Member and Minister of Organization of the Shanghai General Labor Union, and the Standing Committee Member of the Shanghai Labor Union Consolidation Committee. He became more and more diligent in suppressing the communists and leading the labor movement. Although he went through many hardships, he became more and more enthusiastic in his struggle. Therefore, the Communist Party hated him to the bone, and Guo knew this, but he did not care. Suddenly, on the May 5th Memorial Day in 1928, he was ambushed by thugs on Beile Road in the French Concession while on official business, shot in the waist and spine, and sent to Guangci Hospital for treatment. Fortunately, he survived, but the spinal nerve system was severed by the bullet, and the lower body lost all sensation, resulting in disability. The Central Committee approved an annual pension of 400 yuan. After becoming disabled, Guo could not get up and walk, but he could still sit and plan. He still worked hard for the party as before and did not flinch. Therefore, the six district party headquarters in this city repeatedly elected Guo as a supervisory committee member. His belief among comrades can be seen from this. After becoming disabled, Guo deeply felt the difficulties of the times and the national crisis for two years, which was deafening and heartbreaking. He often hated his body for being a burden and consuming the pension. Recently, he heard that the Fumin Hospital established by the Japanese on North Sichuan Road could reconnect the nerve system by surgery, so he resolutely entered the hospital. Comrades and relatives all advised him to stop, because the matter was extremely dangerous, and even the doctors were not sure. Guo did not listen and said that if he could be healthy, his youth could still make a second contribution to the party. Even if he died, it would be better than worrying about old age in bed. He only hoped that all comrades would work hard for the party, and he would have no regrets if he died. The comrades were deeply saddened by his words and the uncertainty of the matter, and accompanied him to the hospital. At 3:00 PM on the 5/30 Memorial Day, the reconnection procedure was performed, and it was completed at 5:00 PM. The sensation in the lower body was restored. Everyone in the hospital was overjoyed. Because Guo had been disabled and economically distressed, his physical condition was weakening. This time, he lost too much blood and collapsed, and he could not be revived until 8:00 PM that night. He had already followed the martyrs. He was injured on the May 5th Memorial Day in 1928 and died on the May 30th Memorial Day in 1930, after two years and twenty-five days. Mr. Guo's death will follow these two anniversaries forever, which can be said to be a fortunate misfortune.

Mr. Guo's family members include his maternal grandmother, who is now 96 years old, his biological mother, who is now 63 years old, his wife, Ms. Ding, who is now 22 years old, and a son named Yongchou (meaning to eternally remember the communists' murder of his father), who is only 4 years old. They were all supported by Mr. Guo.

Posthumous arrangements After Mr. Guo's death, his family was destitute and the responsibility of supporting the elderly and raising children was very heavy. The comrades will organize a funeral committee, report to the municipal party headquarters and request for funeral expenses, and forward it to the central government for a more favorable discussion of the annual pension, which will continue to be received by Guo's son Yongchou in accordance with the regulations. The municipal party headquarters has approved a funeral expense of 500 yuan to handle the funeral affairs first.

Funeral route Mr. Guo's funeral residence is located in Chongye Lane, Yuezhou Road. The funeral will be held at 10:00 AM today (2nd), passing through Yuezhou Road, Zhaofeng Road, Oujia Road, Disiwei Road, North Sichuan Road, Dule'an Road, Donghengbang Road, Baoshan Road, Henan Road, directly to Minguo Road, and walking west to Fangxie Road to the Xieqiao temporary residence in Taizhou Guild Hall.

Official Letter Regarding the Rectification of Silk Cocoon Tax Collection 90

To Mr. Song Ziwen, Minister of Finance: In order to safeguard and rectify the silk cocoon industry, I have specially appointed Wu Longyue as the special financial commissioner of Jiangsu Province. An office has been established in Shanghai. Yesterday, Mr. Wu sent a letter to the Silk Cocoon Industry Association, which reads as follows:

Regarding the silk cocoon taxes, which are a major source of national revenue, over the years, various bureaus have largely failed to strictly implement the regulations and procedures, leading to various malpractices. Dishonest officials and clerks have taken advantage of their positions for personal gain, creating difficulties and making demands. Some have even colluded with merchants to underreport or evade taxes, or use the same invoice multiple times. Such situations are inevitable.

In the case of cunning merchants who seek to benefit themselves and are willing to collude in wrongdoing, genuine and law-abiding merchants are subjected to undue harassment and hardship. Therefore, for the collection of cocoon taxes this year, the original regulations have been revised by this office, and all bureaus are ordered to comply with them, vigorously eliminate long-standing malpractices, and strictly prohibit demands for fees or customary charges associated with tax invoices, in order to achieve rectification.

Furthermore, this office has appointed commissioners to be stationed in Shanghai and Wuxi, the two areas where silk cocoons are most concentrated, to conduct investigations and inspections. With this approach, on the one hand, tax collection is being rectified to prevent fraud and confusion; on the other hand, honest merchants are being protected to facilitate their business operations and alleviate their burdens.

For fear that this is not yet widely known, this letter is being sent to inform all merchants and manufacturers that henceforth, when transporting silk cocoons, after paying the taxes at the point of origin, and passing through the inspection of various authorities, as long as the invoices and goods match and the procedures are complete, verification and stamping will be promptly provided for release. If there is any obstruction or demand for fees, they are permitted to report to this office at any time. Once verified, the relevant officials and clerks will be severely punished to deter greed.

Merchants and manufacturers must also not continue to engage in old malpractices, privately providing customary fees, or colluding in wrongdoing, lest they be held jointly liable. In addition to sending personnel to various locations for secret investigations, you are hereby ordered to comply without fail. Sincerely,

Local News

Fight Among Chauffeurs 95

Caused by Professional Jealousy

Firefighter Helps Fellow Chauffeur

At around 3:00 AM yesterday, a brawl among industry workers occurred at the Xingfa Automobile Company at the intersection of Deswei Road and Tiantong Road. Chauffeur Wei Rongsheng, as well as Yin Maomao, a leader of the Hongkou Fire Brigade, and coppersmith Zhou Zhongsheng were all seriously injured. Fortunately, the First Precinct of the Fifth District Public Security Bureau learned of the incident and dispatched police to arrest all those involved.

The incident stemmed from professional jealousy, the result of a business dispute between the Xingfa and Zhongmei Automobile Companies. The Zhongmei Automobile Company, located at 33 Wusong Road, has been doing fairly well. Especially during horse and dog racing season, it is overwhelmed with business. However, automobiles from other companies, such as Xingfa, have often been found at its door, soliciting customers. On the customer's side, they board any car they see and do not inquire as to whose car it is. However, the owner of Zhongmei feels unhappy about others sharing in his profits, believing that a porridge shop in front of a restaurant is nothing but stealing business. Furthermore, they considered that others were hindering the entry and exit of vehicles and obstructing pedestrian traffic. They frequently used harsh words and sarcasm to order others to leave, but with no result. Instead, the two sides exchanged unpleasant words.

On the day before yesterday, during the Jiangwan horse racing season, both the Zhongmei and Xingfa Automobile Companies sent cars to Jiangwan Road to pick up and drop off customers. Zhongmei chauffeur Geng Longren and Xingfa chauffeur Li Sanxi started a quarrel over competing for passengers, which led to fighting. The situation was very fierce. However, afterwards, they dispersed.

However, at 3:00 AM yesterday, Geng Longren of Zhongmei suddenly led a group of people to argue. Because the two sides had long-standing grudges, the situation quickly escalated. A major brawl broke out. The question of who was right or wrong was irrelevant. Instantly, iron rulers were flying and knives were flashing. Loud shouts were heard by the neighbors. As a result, Wei Rongsheng of the Xingfa Company, Yin Maomao of the Hongkou Fire Brigade, and Zhou Zhongsheng were injured in the head, face, chest, and waist. Several others sustained minor injuries.

The First Precinct of the Fifth District Public Security Bureau learned of the incident and immediately dispatched police to arrest the perpetrators. They were Li Sanxi, Yan Yonggui, Wei Rongsheng, and the defendants Geng Longren, Yin Maomao, Zhou Zhongsheng, Ding Dechang, Zhou Shiyuan, and Shi Yongqing. Of these, Yin, Zhou, and Shi were all employed by the Shenjiawan Fire Brigade and had been invited by the Zhongmei side.
