Art World

That Useless Man – A Casual Comment 192

New Discovery

Chekhov's Unpublished Play During His Lifetime. Tolstoy did not like the kind of plays Chekhov wrote. He once said to Chekhov, "Shakespeare writes bad plays enough, but you write even worse than he does."

This statement is rather surprising, but Tolstoy had his own reasons. Some of Chekhov's published plays are "un-dramatic" dramas, in other words, they are static, lacking dynamic scenes and dramatic plots. Gray characters live gray lives. What moves the reader or audience is not strong and lively action, but weak and mediocre personalities. This is why Chekhov's plays can win the sympathy (and thus the welcome) of readers, and it is also the difference between Chekhov's plays and other people's plays. It is also the main reason why Tolstoy did not like Chekhov's plays.

Chekhov's plays are a genre of their own, just like his novels are a genre of their own. But he did not become such a genre from the beginning of writing plays. It was only after a long period of exploration that he discovered and grasped his unique style. There has been a lot of development and progress in the meantime. This can be seen by looking at his recently discovered manuscript.

A play by Chekhov has recently been discovered, which was not published before. The author probably thought that this work could not be published, so there was no title. Therefore, the original version was published under the title "An Unpublished Play, by Chekhov." Now someone has translated it into English and given it the name "That Useless Man Platonov" (That Wortble

ss Pellow Platonov). For the sake of simplicity, let's call it "That Useless Man."

Those who open this play with the intention of seeing works like "The Cherry Orchard" and "The Three Sisters" will undoubtedly be disappointed, because this is still his immature work. However, if we put aside art, then such a discovery is not common and is invaluable. Moreover, although the technique has not reached perfection, the author's genius has repeatedly revealed itself in the technique, and there are quite a few similarities with his later mature works. This allows us to see the progress of genius.

"That Useless Man Platonov" is the beginning of Chekhov's career as a playwright. This is the result of his first serious attempt to write a play. Although he had tried twice before, as far as we know, both times were with a playful attitude and could not be regarded as serious creations. This play was written in 1880, when Chekhov was only twenty years old and still studying at Moscow University, just starting to submit articles to various magazines to test his literary talent. The signature was the strange "Antosha Cbckhonte." He wrote some humorous essays and short stories, and submitted them to some second- and third-rate magazines. When he wrote this "Platonov," he obviously had great hopes. He dreamed that this play could be performed in a large theater in Moscow, and that he could be transformed overnight from a popular and humble writer to a great writer. However, after he sent the play, the heroine of the theater did not like the play, so Chekhov followed her instructions and began to revise it. But he later put the play aside and stopped the work. Why? Was it because he was busy studying medicine and writing humorous works to make money and had no time for this, or was it because this sensitive and timid young man felt ashamed and angry after being rejected? We don't know. All we know is that nineteen years after Chekhov's death, in 1923, this work was discovered from his old pile of papers, and later published in Moscow.

Technically, this play is incomplete, but in form it is complete. He has a whole story. The content of the story is roughly as follows: Mikhail Vasilyevich Platonov is a rural teacher. His character is noble, and at heart he is moral, but unfortunately he has too strong lust for women, and he is born without the ability to make decisions, without the ability to choose or take. When he encounters women, he has no way out. He can't leave, and he can't stay. He can't have consistent thoughts, and he can't have consistent actions. In short, besides lying softly on the sofa and suffocating himself in that kind of indecisiveness, self-pity, and atmosphere full of eroticism, he has no other way. He is already married. His wife, Sasha, is loyal and gentle, only giving him happiness and not giving him pain, but intellectually, she is much lower than him, so he is dissatisfied with her, and she has no ability to control him, so his lust goes to find another way out, thus stirring up the matter of being in love with three women at the same time.

The first woman is Anna Petrovna, a middle-aged widow who has been interested in him for a long time. He was about to turn to Anna when he suddenly received a letter from Sophia, which made him hesitate. Sophia Ivanovna is Anna's daughter-in-law, whom Platonov fell in love with before he got married. At this time, he felt that things were difficult. Just when he was helpless, suddenly another woman ran in to interfere. This is Maria Yefimovna, also one of his admirers. This time, it was completely ruined. Our Platonov was entangled in this big dispute and could not get out. So in the end, we saw him drunk, surrounded by Anna, Sophia, and Maria. At the same time, his wife, it is said, had swallowed red-headed matches and was dying of poisoning. Sophia was extremely angry at this time, so she picked up a pistol and shot Platonov. She didn't hit him with the first shot (this is an old Russian play trick). She shot him with the second shot, and he died. So this helpless and useless person was given a solution by others.

This play can only be said to be a tragedy, but some parts are really funny. This is Chekhov's characteristic, and it is already revealed in an immature work. Moreover, there are many embryos of later mature works in this play, as if those later mature works all grew out of this play. For example, the protagonist Platonov's hopeless, willless, and neurotic character is very similar to the protagonist of Chekhov's later work "Ivanov." If it weren't for the different plot, we could simply say that "Ivanov" is an adaptation of this play. Furthermore, the Voinitsev aristocratic family, which becomes a large part of the background of the play, and the sentimental atmosphere surrounding the poverty and decline of this family, is obviously the embryo of the basic sentiment revealed in "The Cherry Orchard." There are many such similarities.

It is obvious that all the sentiments, themes, and characters that will be present when the technique matures in the future have already crystallized at the age of twenty. In this respect, "Platonov" has its value.

(B) Drama

Leike (Sven Lange, 1868) His drama lacks vitality and is art for art's sake. The Land, written in 1915, has the passion of battle. His plays include "The Victim" (1896), "The Criminal" (1903), Samson and Delila (1909), "The First Battle" (1929), etc. The last one is about Brandt's childhood life.

"Inside the Wall," written in 1912.

(C) Poetry

Lu'erdan (Yaldemar Rordam, 1872) He is the son of a pastor. He enjoys a high reputation in the Danish poetry world. "Sun and Clouds," written in 1895, is very mediocre. His poems contain many descriptions of sex. Lu'erdan is diligent and studious, but overworks himself and gets a nervous breakdown. Beourelf (1899) was written while he was sick. In 1897, "Three Ropes" and in 1901, "Danish Language." Later, the author got help from friends and went to SchwatZuald and Italy for sightseeing, using this opportunity to recuperate. Later, he recovered his health. In 1902, he wrote a Gudrnud Dyre, which aroused much attention and discussion, and can be said to have caused a sensation for a time. In addition to lyrical poetry, Lu'erdan also wrote novels and plays, but none of them achieved success. He is most famous for his long poems, which are very symbolic and have a deep influence. From 1922 to 1923, he wrote Jens

Hva'sofulvlcjg (I-II). In 1925, he wrote the play "The Luck of Buddha's Pet." He was deeply influenced by Oehle nsc

blager, Gendtving, Wintber, Slaocbm

ann, and other writers. In 1918, he compiled "Selected Poems of Twenty Years" ( ). His main works are "The Old Pastor" (1917), "Pastoral Songs of the City" (1918), "Crossing the Indian Ocean" (1920), "Bird Song" (1924), and "Flower Poems" (1925). The content of the poems is mostly about life overcoming disease, love songs, and homesickness. He describes scenery not only with light, but also with air and color.

Hofmann (Kai Hoffmann, 1874) published "Lily in the Dark" in 1899. The author was deeply influenced by French symbolism. The themes he depicts are the sea, love, and patriotism.

Larsen (Hoger Larsen, 1875) wrote "Land" in 1904 and published "Selected Poems" in 1917. His poems mostly depict rural scenery.

Hansen (Olol Hansen, 1879) translated Dddest and wrote "Riverside" (1913) and "Mill" (1915), etc.

Remestod (Cbristian Rimestod, 1878) was also influenced by French symbolism. The author is also a critic and wrote "A History of New Danish Poetry." Nielsen (L. Nielsen, 1871) is a songwriter.

Regarding "Modern Danish Literature," I have roughly talked about it above. In the Danish literary world, we can summarize it and say that there are two special phenomena. The first is that most writers depict the local customs and the suffering of farmers. The second is that the success of a work is mostly above tens of thousands of words, and the author also spends several years of effort to produce a masterpiece.

Anecdotes from the Literary World 194

Goethe and Schiller's Friendship

Goethe first met Schiller in 1779, when he was thirty years old, but he didn't have the opportunity to speak until the summer of 1788, when he was thirty-nine years old, when he was playing with King Taiyin in Roteltertd.

After that, their friendship never left a warm state until death. Therefore, the depth and enthusiasm of their friendship is rare in the history of all literary figures. However, they had opposite personalities and circumstances. In Germany at that time, it could be said that they were in the position of twenty competitors.

Due to the difference in their personalities, the same appearance was completely different. Goethe had a broad forehead and sunken, huge eyes. His dignified appearance could make people think of his greatness at a glance. Schiller's appearance seemed to be the opposite of Goethe's. He had a thin face, but his eyes were bright and shiny, and his head and neck were thin and long. When he walked with his head down, he looked like a walking camel.

Goethe liked cleanliness, fresh air, and wanted to live in a well-lit house, but Schiller, on the contrary, couldn't start writing without the smell of rotten apples.

Goethe wanted to start writing in the clear morning, while Schiller had to be stimulated by coffee and champagne in the middle of the night before he could start writing.

Schiller was ten years younger than Goethe, but he died before Goethe. He died on May 9, 1805, at the age of sixty-four. At that time, the Weimar Theater stopped to express its condolences. When people heard this unfortunate news, everyone was amazed at the death of this genius.

At that time, Goethe had been bedridden for a long time, so he could not go to comfort his sick old friend. Until after Schiller's death, no one dared to report to Goethe, because he himself was old and bedridden, and could not bear the grief of the death of a beloved friend. At that time, the people living with him got the news and went outside to discuss whether to report it, but Goethe had already noticed something strange and asked,

"I know, is Schiller in danger?" After he said this sentence, he sighed incessantly. That night, the old Goethe's room was particularly quiet. The next morning, when a woman came to Goethe's room, he asked sadly,

"Yesterday I thought Schiller was in danger, is it true?"

At that time, the woman saw Goethe's concerned face and didn't know how to answer. So, unknowingly, she covered her face with a handkerchief and cried.

Goethe saw such an attitude, and of course understood completely, so he shouted,

"Ah, Schiller is dead?"

"Yes,"

The woman answered while crying.

"Ah, Schiller is dead?"

Goethe shouted twice in a row, and then used his hand to cover his eyes, which were about to burst into tears.

Goethe lived two years longer than Schiller. He died on March 2, 1832 and was buried next to Schiller's tomb. Although they have died, the shells of their souls are still placed together. (Ping)

The Female Knight of Chongjiang

Episode 2: Burning of the Han Family Village, Playing for Three Consecutive Days Starting Today at the Central Grand Theater

Have you gentlemen read the novel "The Female Knight of Chongjiang," published by Da Yi Bookstore, which describes Gu Ming's death before arrival? If you have, then that immortal union of qin and sword, as if attached yet detached, and all the dragon-like leaps and tiger-like bounds, the martial skills and swordsmanship, must often swirl in your mind, indelible. Now, it vividly appears on the silver screen, with the delicate, agile, and quick-witted heroine, Xu Qin Fang, playing the role. Her performance is lifelike and charmingly adorable, truly making it worthwhile to watch. Have you gentlemen seen the first episode of this film, "Rampage at the Shelin Temple"?

If you have already seen it, then surely you urgently need to see the sequel. If, because you are busy, you missed the opportunity, then do not inadvertently miss this episode, "Burning of the Han Family Village," a wonderfully exciting and tightly packed drama filled with significant revelations.

News from the Publishing World

New China Company Announces: The "New China Complete Telegraphic Code," was yesterday granted Registration License No. 517 by Zhang Wohua, Permanent Vice Minister of the Ministry of Interior. It is used by many in various ports. For example, Shanghai Sanyo Industrial Company, Harbin Bank of China, Nanjing Central Party Department Organization Department, Qingdao Ministry of Industry and Commerce Commodity Inspection Bureau, Shaoguan Yuehan Railway Engineering Bureau, etc. have all adopted it effectively. The book is available for consignment sale at all radio stations across the country, and the Shanghai Commercial Press also sells it on consignment. The general distributor is the New China Engineering Company, No. 7 Ningbo Road. Each volume sells for one dollar. Users save as much as several hundred dollars per month, demonstrating its effectiveness. The "People's Talk Monthly" Publishing House announces: This magazine is a combination of young authors such as Nie Haifan, Liu Gongren, and Wu Yuanqing. It has been in preparation for several months and is a purely open academic research publication. The inaugural issue was published yesterday and contains columns such as translated essays, literary criticism, and more. It is currently sold on consignment at the Xinyue Bookstore on Fourth Road, the Xinyuzhou Bookstore on North Sichuan Road, and university bookstores.

Medical News 209

Famous Doctor Gao Yingshi Announces: This doctor has long been renowned in Songjiang. Fellow villagers in Shanghai are familiar with my rich experience and have persuaded me to practice medicine in Shanghai. I have now established a clinic at No. 16 Taiyuan Fang, West Zilaihuo Street, French Concession. Consultation fees are waived for the poor and sick.

Chen Jinjie, Specialist in Traumatology from Xinghua, Announces: This doctor's family has resided in Xinghua for generations, and my family has practiced traditional traumatology for over ten generations. My ancestors used surgery and secret medicinal products to save countless lives, earning renown throughout the north and south of the Yangtze River. I inherit my ancestors' aspirations and have a heart for helping the world. I have been practicing medicine for over twenty years, meticulously studying and striving for perfection. For all cases of falls, blows, knife and axe injuries, severed tendons, fractured bones, penetrating wounds, unstoppable bleeding, waist and rib pain, palpitations, and stabbing pain in the heart and abdomen, I do not use needles, sutures, massage, or plasters. I treat with plasters, adhesives, elixirs, and powders, and also perform surgery. Pain stops immediately, and the skin, flesh, tendons, and bones self-connect and self-heal. The effects are immediate and verified as miraculous. Now, fellow villagers and relatives in Shanghai have repeatedly invited me to Shanghai to practice medicine and provide universal relief to patients. Please visit No. 1 Guling Road, Public Concession. Time: 10:00 AM to 12:00 PM, 2:00 PM to 4:00 PM. Also selling plasters, adhesives, elixirs, and powders.
